Sakahara was also invited to attend the meeting, which did not break up until dawn on the 17th. Dohihara and the others then went to the Tokiwa Hotel to rest. On the evening of the 17th, these individuals gathered again at the Japanese Consulate General for a meeting that lasted late into the night. The content of the two meetings was extremely secret. It is reported that Dohihara left Tianjin yesterday (the 19th), with some saying he went to Peiping and others saying he returned to Changchun. It is unknown which is true. In any case, the cholera bacteria of Tianjin are quietly growing and spreading, and there will inevitably be a day of massive vomiting and diarrhea.

According to a certain military expert, the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, nominally a regiment, actually consists of less than 1,500 men, with about 2,000 veterans in the area. Our troops stationed in the four rural districts of Tianjin are already prepared. Furthermore, the plainclothes teams organized by general traitors are all rabble. The Japanese are only using them as a fuse. However, one thing is particularly noteworthy: after the Tianjin Incident of the year before last, the Japanese secretly purchased land between Haiguang Temple and Bali Terrace Fort to the south, ostensibly establishing industrial companies and racetracks, but in reality, they have invisibly built a large airfield. According to information leaked by the Japanese side, there are two medium-sized fighter planes in the hangar of the airfield, and two large fighter planes are stored in the Japanese barracks at Haiguang Temple. The airfield is now a forbidden zone for the Japanese, and we have no way to investigate its reality. Here is an investigation report on the traitorous plainclothes team: (1) The background of the plainclothes team is two specialists dispatched by the Japanese Army Ministry to disrupt North China: Okazaki Tetsuichi and Hasegawa; (2) The leader of the plainclothes team is Hao Peng, the former Finance Director of Zhili Province, who was arrested in Peiping on the 10th of this month; (3) The cadres of the plainclothes team are Zhang Bi and Zhu Zijun, formerly regimental commanders of the Zhili-Shandong Army; Liu Yide, who is currently recruiting bandits in Dezhou and Cangzhou; Han Guodong, formerly a brigade commander of the Zhili-Shandong Army; Liu Xuehai, formerly a battalion commander of the Zhili-Shandong Army; and He Zhongsan, formerly an adjutant to Liu Guitang; (4) The organization of the plainclothes team is named the North China People's Autonomous National Salvation Army, with Hao Peng as commander-in-chief, Zhang Bi as deputy commander-in-chief, Zhu Zijun as chief of staff, Liu Yide as adjutant general, Han Guodong as commander-in-chief, Liu Xuehai as commander of the first army, He Zhongsan as commander of the second army, and Feng Lindong as commander of the third army; (5) Strength: The confirmed number of those lying in wait in the Japanese Concession is about one thousand; it is said that there are ten thousand in the outer counties, but this is exaggerated and unreliable; (6) Economic sources: Hao Peng borrowed 20,000 dollars from Okazaki in his name as secret operating expenses; after the launch, Okazaki is responsible for military pay, with Hasegawa and others signing as witnesses; (7) Weapons: The plainclothes team lying in wait in the Japanese Concession currently has one rifle for every three people; when the launch occurs, Okazaki will supply a large quantity. After Hao Peng was captured in Peiping on the 10th of this month, our local authorities have been severely cracking down on the remaining traitors. These individuals know that their crimes are heinous and are fleeing into hiding. (January 20th)

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (18)

Japanese Request for Instructions After Submission to the Assembly 95

"Matsuoka": I would like to first express the Japanese delegation's gratitude to the Chairman of the Administrative Council for his sincerity in earnestly seeking a solution to our current dispute. We are extremely grateful for the Chairman's efforts and his capable guidance. Regarding the current issues before the Administrative Council, I firmly believe that they should be considered by the Administrative Council itself. The Administrative Council has received the report from the Investigation Committee, and the report also proposes several solutions to the Administrative Council. However, these points are merely suggestions. In the view of the Japanese government, the Administrative Council should conduct its own research on the issue and seek ways for both sides to come closer. The suggestions made by the Investigation Committee to the Administrative Council cannot be easily agreed to, and it is also questionable whether the Investigation Committee has the authority to make suggestions or issue conclusions. In my observation, the Investigation Committee does not have such authority. The Japanese government has submitted a memorandum of opinion to the Administrative Council regarding the report, clearly explaining all the points that disagree with the report in detail. The Chinese government has repeatedly stated that it will gladly accept any proposals from the League of Nations, but in fact, up to this point, China has taken no action other than accusations and condemnations. As the Chairman said, the Chinese government's attitude towards the report, other than agreeing in principle to the third point, "any solution should comply with the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Washington Nine-Power Treaty," is not clearly expressed. The government represented by the Chinese representatives has not fulfilled its obligations under those treaties. During the Administrative Council meetings in October, November, and December of last year, the Japanese government expressed its willingness to engage in direct negotiations with the Chinese government based on the five principles proposed by the Chinese government. The Japanese government firmly believed at the time that this suggestion was the most concrete way to seek a satisfactory solution to the entire issue, and its spirit has also been recognized by the Investigation Committee report, as the Investigation Committee advocates direct negotiations. Unfortunately, in the autumn of last year, the Administrative Council did not agree with Japan's proposal, and as a result, the situation in Manchuria developed according to its natural course. To this day, its status is no longer reversible. Since the Chairman has proposed submitting the entire case to the Assembly for resolution, the discussion will probably proceed according to Article 15 of the Covenant. Regarding this proposal, I can only express my personal opinion at this time and telegraph Tokyo for instructions. Once the instructions are received, I will notify the Chairman immediately. I firmly believe that if this case is submitted to the Assembly for resolution in accordance with Article 15 of the Covenant, the Assembly's responsibility should be to do everything possible to seek a solution that both sides can compromise on. If that is the case, then whether the case is resolved in accordance with Article 11 of the Covenant or in accordance with Article 15, paragraph 3, it will still lead to the same destination by different routes. This is my personal opinion. Furthermore, I believe that any solution that is not agreed to by both parties to the dispute cannot be considered satisfactory. For such an important matter, it is impossible to force any party to accept a solution. The League of Nations will certainly not seek the complete agreement of both parties, and I certainly cannot express my approval until complete agreement is obtained. This is why the Japanese government submitted reservations to Article 13 of the Covenant this spring. It goes without saying that the establishment of world peace is the common desire of all member states of the League of Nations. The purpose of the League of Nations itself is also there. Japan is no less devoted to this desire than any other country. We do need peace, but what we need is not just peace on paper, but peace based on facts. The various actions taken by Japan since last year have been based on this creed. Japan firmly believes that the only way to guarantee the establishment of solid peace in East Asia is to continue to proceed in accordance with Japan's policy of officially recognizing the new state of "Manchukuo." This is the only and reliable way to achieve our shared desire for consistent peace. As for the points mentioned by the Chairman, I reserve the right to speak at the next meeting.

"Chairman": If my understanding is correct, the Japanese representative intends to request instructions from his government on this matter. I wonder how long it will take for the request and the reply to be exchanged.

"Matsuoka": Although I cannot determine a specific date, I expect to receive a reply tomorrow, or at the latest, Monday.

China Agrees to Transfer to the Assembly 96

"Representative Gu": I would like to express my support for the Chairman's proposal to transfer the Investigation Committee's report and the debates between China and Japan to the Assembly for resolution. The Chinese delegation fully agrees that this case should be resolved by the Assembly, as the special Assembly has officially been given all the facts pertaining to this dispute. Regarding the remarks I made in the past few days, the Chairman pointed out that I have not yet indicated the Chinese government's views on the last two chapters of the report, which is true. Among the ten principles in the report, the third is one that China can fully agree with, and regarding the other principles, China reserves the right to express its opinions later. The reason for this is that, first, the responsibility for finding a way to resolve the case now belongs to the Assembly, and as far as I know, the representatives of the Administrative Council are also willing to express their opinions in the Assembly, so I also wish to reserve the Chinese government's opinions for the Assembly meetings. Second, the reason why I did not express the Chinese government's opinions is due to the attitude of the Japanese representative, whose first speech did not show any trace of respect for the fundamental principles of peace and international obligations upon which the League of Nations is based, as the Chairman had hoped. After listening carefully to his speech, I felt that there was no intention of making any concessions. Therefore, I felt that even if the Chinese government's views on the other parts of the report were expressed, it would not help matters. Just now, the Japanese representative suddenly made the first concession to me in fifteen months and asked me to speak first. At that time, not only I personally, but also all the representatives of the Administrative Council, had a kind of hope, but this hope was like a flash in the pan, fleeting in an instant. My failure to accept the Japanese representative's kind intentions was not because I did not appreciate the spirit of his concession, but because I hoped that this concession was only the beginning, and that after I reciprocated his spirit of concession, the Japanese representative might make a second concession and express at least in principle acceptance of the third principle of Chapter IX of the Investigation Committee's report, acknowledging that any solution should be in accordance with the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Nine-Power Treaty. I fully hoped that the Japanese representative would certainly accept this principle, as China and Japan are both signatories to those treaties and both members of the League of Nations. However, my hopes have been dashed. The Japanese representative did not make a second concession, but instead went backwards and made accusations against the Chinese government, which were completely unfounded, because China has always fully complied with the above-mentioned treaties and has never violated them, as the members of the Administrative Council are well aware. However, the Japanese representative has expressed one point, which is that Japan has recognized "Manchukuo" and that any peace, if it is a true peace, must be based on facts. But should we only pursue facts here, and set aside all justice and the common interests of world peace? Should the organization of the League of Nations only recognize facts, and not uphold the peace, justice, and legality upon which it is based? What China opposes is the idea of ​​creating a solution based on the existing fait accompli. The Chinese government will gladly accept any solution based on principles that we all accept. The Chinese government will also gladly accept any solution based on facts created in accordance with the provisions of international treaties. However, as the Japanese representative said, a solution to this case should be based on recognizing "Manchukuo", then China cannot accept it at all. The Japanese representative expressed doubts about whether the Investigation Committee could offer its views and suggestions. This matter can be explained by the Investigation Committee itself or by the members of the Administrative Council and the procedures of the Administrative Council, as some of you have been representatives of the Administrative Council since the establishment of the League of Nations, and your experience is far greater than mine. Finally, I would like to reiterate my agreement with the Chairman's proposal to transfer the Investigation Committee's report and the opinions of China and Japan to the Assembly for resolution as soon as possible.

"Matsuoka": I would like to express my gratitude to my Chinese friend, the Chinese representative, for his kind intentions towards me. However, I must reserve the right to criticize what he has said. The Chinese representative still has doubts about my use of the word "facts". Now, please allow me to clarify. By facts, I mean all facts, including the League of Nations, all treaties, and everything that exists in the world.

Decision to Reconvene Next Monday 97

The Chairman said, the representatives of the Administrative Council have heard the Japanese representative's request and the time limit, so that he can ask Tokyo to submit the report and the opinions of both parties to the Assembly meeting. Is the Administrative Council willing to allow that request? Does anyone object? (No one objects.) In that case, will the Japanese representative be able to receive a reply from Tokyo by tomorrow afternoon?

"Matsuoka": I will do my best, but I cannot determine a specific time limit.

"Chairman": In that case, to be on the safe side, we might as well set the meeting for eleven o'clock next Monday.

"Matsuoka": We must understand that this is a very serious issue for Japan. I certainly cannot speak for the government, so I cannot determine the time limit now, but I will do my best to get a reply from the government as soon as possible.

"Chairman": If the representatives of the Administrative Council can agree, then we might as well decide to include this case on the agenda for eleven o'clock next Monday. There will be no meeting tomorrow, so our discussion of this case has been postponed until eleven o'clock on Monday (the 28th). (End)

Public Memorial Service for Battalion Commander An in Peiping

An's Coffin to Be Transported Back to Baoding for Burial 98

Beijing Correspondence: The coffin of An Dexin, the battalion commander of the Ninth Brigade who died with Yuguan, has been transported to Peiping by the military authorities and temporarily placed in the Qingzhen Mosque in Jiaozihu Tong. On the 19th, people from all walks of life held a public memorial service. Many military and political figures and fellow Muslims attended. Details are as follows:

Situation of the Funeral Hall 99

An's coffin was placed in the two palace rooms of the mosque. A memorial shed was erected high in the courtyard, with elegiac couplets and wreaths sent by various circles, about a hundred items. Wan Fulin, Shao Wenkai, Bao Yulin, and others all sent elegiac couplets and wreaths. Other groups and Muslim organizations also sent elegiac couplets and wreaths, a dazzling array, with almost no space on the walls. An incense table was set up in front of the spirit, with elegiac couplets from Zhang Xueliang hanging on both sides, with the text: "Guarding the land together, the vanguard makes me the spirit of the three armies," "Wielding a spear, thinking bravely and decisively, history transmits this name for a hundred generations." The scene in the room was solemn, inspiring thoughts of reverence.

The Process of Paying Tribute 100

That afternoon, the Muslim Ahong recited scriptures, and representatives of Wan Fulin, Bao Yulin, Shao Wenkai, and others paid tribute. Other groups and citizens also came to pay tribute in an endless stream. Because Muslims do not value grand ceremonies, there were no various musical instruments. Those who came to pay tribute only bowed three times to the spirit. Even at six o'clock in the afternoon, there were still people coming to pay tribute, because the citizens all felt that Battalion Commander An had sacrificed himself for the country, so many braved the snow to come.

An's Brother Speaks 101

According to An's brother, Deming, "My (An's) brother sent his family back to his hometown during the critical period of national crisis to prepare to devote himself to the country. Afterwards, he wrote to his family, saying that the foreign insult is becoming increasingly urgent, and I am prepared to guard the land for the country and put life and death aside. All matters at home can be taken care of by the eldest brother (i.e., An Deming). At the time, I thought he was being paranoid, but I didn't expect this to happen. Now there is still an eighty-year-old mother and a brother at home, and he left behind a wife, two daughters, and a son (his wife is thirty-eight years old, the eldest daughter is thirteen years old, the second daughter is eight years old, and the youngest son is only three years old). The family has always run a small business and has no large property. Commander He gave him one hundred yuan for funeral expenses," he said. According to An's classmate, Han Shucai, "An was a student of the sixth class of the Infantry Department of the Northeast Military Academy and graduated in the summer of the sixteenth year. Later, he served as a major battalion commander of the 23rd Division of the 29th Army and adjutant general of this division. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, it was reorganized into the 9th Independent Brigade of the Infantry, and An served as the lieutenant colonel battalion commander of the first battalion of the 626th Regiment of the brigade. This time, Battalion Commander An defended Yuguan to the death, bravely fought the enemy, took the lead, and died unexpectedly, which is a pity."

Coffin Returns to Baoding 102

Because of Muslim customs, the coffin cannot be kept for a long time, so it was decided to be transported from the original site at seven o'clock on the 20th to the West Railway Station and transported to Baoding by the 22nd Pingguan train at ten o'clock in the morning. It can be buried on the 21st or 22nd. In addition to his brother An Deming, several teachers from the Qingzhen Mosque in Qinhuangdao and Han Dongcai, a representative of the Muslims in Peiping, accompanied him back to his hometown. It is reported that various groups and all members of the Muslim community in Peiping plan to hold a large-scale memorial service in Zhongshan Park in the near future. (20th)

Jiangbei Affected by Heavy Snow

Traffic Disrupted, Boats and Cars Crash, Commerce Depressed, Finance Stagnant

Zhenjiang Correspondence: Jiangbei has had continuous heavy snow for days. On the 19th, all ships and cars were suspended. Those traveling from Zhenjiang to Yangzhou could only cross the river by sailboat. After crossing the river, they could only see rickshaws struggling in the wind and snow. In the fields, the snow was several feet deep and boundless. The 28-mile car road took four hours to reach. The north wind howled, and it felt like a knife scraping the face. Snowflakes went straight into the car compartment, and the passengers' clothes and shoes were covered with an inch of snow. Their beards and eyebrows were white, and their hands and feet were stiff. Many telegraph poles along the road were broken, and telephones in Yangzhou and telegrams in Zhenjiang and Qingjiang were not working. Ice floes flowed down the canal, blocking Sanwan, and the entire river was frozen. All small ferries were suspended, and traffic on both sides of the Yangtze River was completely disrupted for a while. Vegetable fields were submerged under more than two feet of snow, and farmers could not dig them up. The city was already short of vegetarian food. Vendors could not buy or sell due to the snow, and the poorest people cried out in the streets, which was extremely miserable. Business was slow in all shops, and many money houses went bankrupt. Financial turnover was sluggish, and people's livelihoods were in distress. As the end of the old year approached, the various educational, charitable, and public welfare institutions in Yangzhou relied on the salt business to maintain their operations, amounting to five or six hundred thousand yuan, and the number of people who depended on it for a living was no less than a thousand families and ten thousand people. However, the Salt Transport Department suddenly sent personnel to the Japan Coast Public Office the day before yesterday to investigate the expenses of the past ten years. It is said that someone was dissatisfied with the public office and offered this advice to the Salt Transport Department, which wanted to know the truth, so it ordered an audit. Whether there were any abuses would be known as soon as the investigation was conducted. However, at the time of the economic closing of the lunar year, all the books were sealed up for investigation, and all appropriations for the various institutions for the end of the year were suspended, causing great pain to tens of thousands of people. It is also reported that long-distance buses and lighters in Yangzhou have had accidents and sunk. However, the snow on the bus road was cleared yesterday and should be open to traffic today. (19th)

Songjiang Asks for Reduction of Arrears in Grain Tax Due to Snow

The grain tax is increased by two yuan per stone. Previously, the directors of the property office of this county, He Zihua, Cai Guang, and Wu Qian, telegraphed the Ministry of Finance and the provincial government, stating that the price of rice had fallen and the people's strength was low, requesting an exemption. The reply was received that after the flood of the year before last, finances were difficult, and the provincial treasury's revenue was not sufficient. The Ministry of Finance was requested to approve a one-year extension. As for this year's rice and grain, it is now approved for circulation, and the value is expected to increase, so the request for exemption should not be considered. Now, the directors stated that the grain tax has been increased and the burden on the people has been increased for two years, and the people are feeling pain from the extension this year. Because the above order cannot be resisted, they have to endure the pain and pay it. However, a small number of families with slightly more financial resources can pay it, while the economically weak households cannot pay it on time and are subject to late fees. The investigation of taxes and duties is an obligation that the people should fulfill, and households that pay late should be subject to penalties. However, this late fee is increased by one-tenth of the autumn quota. If it is paid after the deadline, each stone will be collected at seven yuan and nine angles, including collection fees, and within the two-yuan discount, there will be a late fee of two angles. The government has repeatedly increased the grain tax without considering the people's hardships, and this late fee is added to the burden on the people, causing dissatisfaction. The directors are deeply saddened and cannot remain silent, so they specially telegraphed for verification, urgently ordering the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance and the Songjiang Finance Bureau to deduct this late fee when calculating the two-yuan grain tax to comfort the people and appease public opinion. They are waiting for orders.

Robbery and Kidnapping Case in Lishu Township 103

Eight bandits suddenly came to Sunjia Village, Lishu Township, Suzhou County, on the night of the 21st, armed with guns, broke into the house of He Genshui, wantonly searched and robbed, losing about three hundred yuan. Before leaving, they tied up Zhou's wife, Chen, and left a note demanding 5,000 yuan for ransom.

Completion of the Sujia Road Project 104

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction has been constructing the Suwu section (between Suzhou and Wujiang) of the Sujia Road for half a year. All earthwork has been completed early, and the pavement is now being laid. The entire project can be completed by the end of this month. The Baodai Bridge outside Fengmen has also been completed. The bridge is more than thirty feet long, and the project is quite large, being the largest bridge on the entire road.

Approval for Reduced Collection of Surveying Fees 105

The County Finance Bureau received an order to levy a surveying donation of one angle per mu on the additional land price tax. After the county residents Qian Ding and others repeatedly appealed to the province for a reduction, an order was received approving a reduction of 2.5 cents, and the actual levy will be 7.5 cents per mu.

Nanhui

Resolution of the Nanhui-Fengxian Boundary Issue 106

The Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, based on the joint report of the county magistrates of Nanhui and Fengxian, Wu Xie, to the Provincial Committee, regarding the Nanhui-Fengxian boundary issue, repeatedly convened local people from the two counties to discuss and decide on five proposed solutions. Afterwards, the Nanhui side considered that the first proposal to divide the former Taiping Township into an autonomous region was not necessary in fact and argued for a long time, which was difficult to agree on. The rest were largely settled. As for Fengxian's request to divide part of Songjiang's Yexie Township and Nanhui's request to divide part of Shanghai's Chenhang Township, both were abandoned. The jointly drafted proposal was submitted for approval, and yesterday, the county magistrates of Nanhui and Fengxian, Wu Xie, and others were ordered to approve the proposal. However, regarding the first proposal to establish an autonomous region, the Nanhui County Government was ordered to re-deliberate according to law.

Wuxi

Conspiracy of Adulterers to Murder the Husband 107

The twenty-ninth detachment of the merchant corps in Meicun Town, District 12 (Qinbo City), was headed by a certain Qiang. Four patrol officers were stationed there, one of whom, a squad leader named Chen Lixian, was from Xuzhou and around forty years old. He had married a woman last February. She was young and attractive, with a naturally flirtatious disposition. She exchanged amorous glances with a soldier from the third platoon stationed there, who was flattered and became entangled with her. Chen's wife accommodated them all, dispensing her favors equally, sharing the pleasures of spring with the third platoon soldier. Eventually, scandalous rumors spread, and Chen became aware of the affair, leading to frequent quarrels. Unexpectedly, the adulterers, emboldened by lust, plotted to murder Chen to ensure lasting peace and comfort. Yesterday, Chen's body was suddenly discovered in the reed marshes a hundred paces from the Qiang family bridge. There were no visible injuries, but blood flowed from all seven orifices. Chen's wife and the third platoon soldier had also disappeared simultaneously. Afterward, the head of the merchant corps, Qiang, led his members in a thorough search for the fugitives, but to no avail. Qiang has decided to come to the city today with Yuan Ying-san from Tuzhi to report to the county court, request an inquest, and inform the merchant guild, which will then report to the county government, urging them to order the apprehension of the fugitives.

Rice Boat Capsizes, Two Lives Tragically Lost 111

At around 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, south of San Dui Town, District Six of the county, a Xinghua rice boat was passing by when it suddenly encountered a hurricane and capsized. There were a husband and wife and three boys on board. People tried their best to rescue them, and the three children were saved, but the husband and wife could not be found. It wasn't until the next morning that their bodies were discovered floating on the water. How tragic!

Hong Family Robbed in Sanyang Township 112

More than ten bandits suddenly came to the home of farmer Hong Fu-shou in Sanyang Township, District Ten of the county, the night before last. Wu Chao-chu Talks About Britain's Appeasement of Japan 119

Failure of Mediation is Better Than Delaying, and Urges the Chinese People to Quickly Seek Self-Salvation

The New Voice Society reported that Central Committee member Wu Chao-chu gave an interview to reporters yesterday, stating that Britain's recent attitude of appeasing Japan is an inevitable trend in its psychology and interests. He also advised the Chinese people to awaken, abandon their past reliance on the League of Nations, and quickly seek self-salvation. His remarks are recorded in detail below.

Britain's Appeasement of Japan 120

Before beginning the interview, Wu smiled and said to the reporters, "What you want to ask is no different from giving me a test." He then answered the reporters' questions, saying that Britain's recent appeasement of Japan in the League of Nations meeting was partly due to the need to deal with the issue of war debts to the United States. However, he believed that Britain's appeasement of Japan had a natural tendency. (1) As we know, although the Anglo-Japanese Alliance has been canceled, it is unprecedented for Britain to form an alliance with a certain country during peacetime. Twenty years ago, Britain was willing to form an alliance with Japan, which was due to dealing with Russia. However, another reason was that British officials and the public had a considerable emotional connection with Japan at that time. This kind of emotional effect has not been completely eliminated to this day. The British Conservative Party has this kind of psychology and is greatly influenced by it. Therefore, Britain's current defense is its main reason. Most people believe that since the Anglo-Japanese Alliance has been terminated, the close relationship between Britain and Japan has also been cut off. In fact, this is not the case. The cancellation of the alliance is only a kind of diplomatic policy. (2) Britain's relationship with the Northeast Three Provinces is not significant. The more important relationship is with other parts of China. At present, Britain does not have the power to stop violent Japan. Therefore, it has no choice but to allow Japan to carry out aggression in places that have a smaller relationship with itself, and Britain's losses are lighter. All of these are important in terms of psychology and interests.

Seek Self-Salvation Quickly 121

Wu continued, "Judging from the recent mediation situation of the League of Nations on the Sino-Japanese issue, if it fails, and a report is prepared in accordance with Article 15, Section 4 of the Covenant, it is difficult for us to speculate whether this report will be beneficial to our country. Whatever the League of Nations can do, it can be ignored. In general, it is better than the current situation of delay and can awaken the illusions of those who have relied on the League of Nations in the past. The only way is to seek self-salvation."

The League of Nations is Like This 122

At this point, Wu recalled his criticism of the League of Nations a year ago, saying, "The League of Nations is indeed a good international organization, but everything depends on various countries. Today, it is possible to solve the major Sino-Japanese dispute with this organization that has no money and no power? The League of Nations is just a child. Fifty years later, it will be better than today. However, it is difficult to predict whether this child will become a pillar of society or just thatch after he grows up. At present, it is just a place for propaganda and stating public reason."

Wu Will Enter Beijing 123

Military Committee Chairman Jiang invited Wu to enter Beijing. Reporters asked Wu if this was true. Wu said that it was indeed true and that he would go to Beijing when necessary.

Spirits are Encouraged, Vow to Resist to the Death

The Nationalist Society reported that the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association had previously allocated 10,000 yuan to He Zhuguo's troops and remitted it to the Tianjin Local Association for distribution. Yesterday, the association received a telegram from Zhang Boling, chairman of the Tianjin Local Association, informing that personnel had been sent to Qinhuangdao to provide practical comfort. The entire army cheered upon hearing that Shanghai had allocated money for comfort, and they all automatically shouted to resist to the death. Zhu Jiahua Talks 125

The Ministry of Communications Consolidates and Develops the Situation

Since arriving in Shanghai a few days ago, Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Communications and Minister of Education, was interviewed by reporters from the New Sound Society yesterday at the Cangzhou Hotel. When asked about all the problems of the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Education, he gave detailed answers as follows.

Consolidating the Post Office 126

According to Zhu, the merger of the Postal Remittance and Savings Bureau has already been decided, and the reorganization of the Post Office will still be carried out according to the previously announced plan. As for the reasons for the reorganization, on the one hand, due to the Northeast issue and the military actions in the bandit areas, the postal economy has suffered a great blow. Therefore, in order to maintain the domestic postal service, it was decided to immediately engage in retrenchment. All those who used to receive salaries without working will be dismissed to save money. In addition, in remote areas such as Yunnan and Xinjiang, due to inconvenient transportation, multiple transshipments, and many difficulties, and at the same time, the currency system in the border provinces is subject to decline, but the post office must still provide normal services and had to endure painful sacrifices in order to maintain transportation in the border provinces. All of these points must be reorganized and reformed in order to develop.

China Merchants Plan 127

After the China Merchants Bureau was taken back under state management, the board of directors and the general manager have been actively proceeding. First, they will eliminate accumulated malpractices and reduce staff, which is also an important plan to save money and increase practical benefits. The reorganization plan is still being drafted in detail by General Manager Liu. The funds for the reorganization may be issued in public bonds or allocated by the Ministry of Finance, but it has not been completely decided yet. Up to recently, half of the shares have been recovered, but this will end at the end of February. As for the cases of fraud by Chen Fumu and Li Guojie, they have been handed over to the court for public trial and are already a legal matter. The Ministry of Communications will no longer consult on them, but the contract with the China Business Company will definitely be canceled.

Sino-British Telecommunications 128

It is also said that the Sino-British telecommunications planned by the International Radio Station, after repeated negotiations between the Ministry of Communications and the Marconi Company, all the materials and equipment will be borrowed from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund. It is expected that the installation will be completed more than half a year later. The implementation of this communication will definitely further improve Sino-British relations.

Mackay Contract 129

As for the Mackay Contract, because China suffered too much loss from it, after it was discovered, serious negotiations were conducted and efforts were made to cancel it. However, after repeated negotiations between the Ministry of Communications and the company, because it had been formally concluded, progress was more difficult. However, the Ministry of Communications will definitely take into account our country's sovereignty and continue to negotiate in order to achieve the goal of cancellation.

Financial Unification 130

He continued that the Ministry of Finance's proposed convening of various ministries and departments to jointly discuss the issue of financial unification has been completely decided in principle. However, the implementation methods and procedures are more complicated and difficult to achieve in a short period of time. As for the position of Minister of Education, since Weng Wenhao was appointed to take over, he initially firmly declined, but after being retained by the central government, he agreed to take the position. However, due to the tension in North China, he is maintaining school affairs in Ping and has not been able to come south to take office. During this period, he can only temporarily serve as a substitute.

Song Ziwen Returned to Beijing Last Night 131

Song Ziwen, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, arrived in Shanghai by train from Beijing on the morning of the 18th. Because he had completed his official business, he returned to Beijing by night train last night.

The City's Labor Community Held a Representative Congress Yesterday 137

More Than Twenty Important Cases on Resisting Japan and Defending Against Aggression Were Approved

It Was Resolved to Raise Funds to Build a "Shanghai Workers" Aircraft

At the Same Time, the Second Session of New Executive and Supervisory Committee Members Was Elected

Dagong News Agency reported that the Shanghai General Labor Union, because the violent Japanese had already occupied the Northeast and were again disturbing Yuguan, with the country and its people in imminent danger, convened a representative congress of all labor unions in the city at 2:00 PM yesterday to collectively discuss the anti-Japanese policy. More than 400 representatives from over sixty unions attended and passed important cases such as resisting Japan and defending against aggression. Finally, the executive and supervisory committee members of the General Labor Union were re-elected. The details are recorded below:

Meeting Place Arrangement: The meeting place was held at the Xiaoximen Juvenile Propaganda Corps. Above the entrance to the meeting place, a white cloth banner with the words "Shanghai City Labor Community Representative Congress" was hung high. When each representative entered the meeting, they presented their attendance certificate and signed their name in order before taking their seats. Slogans such as "Urge the Government to Send Troops to Recover the Lost Territory of the Northeast," "Reduce Spending and Aid the Volunteer Army," and "Concentrate Efforts and Unite to Resist Japan" were posted around the meeting place. Inside the venue, silk worker Boy Scouts maintained order.

Attending Representatives: More than sixty labor unions including postal service, postal service workers, Fourth District cigarette, Sixth District water and electricity, First District water and electricity, Fifth District cigarette, China Merchants Bureau Fifth Wharf, Shanghai-Ningbo Steamboat Tea Room, Municipal Dyeing Industry, Steamboat Timber Industry, Fourth District Silk Reeling, Seventh District Cotton Weaving, First District Shipbuilding, Pharmaceutical Industry, Pharmaceutical Industry, etc. attended. More than four hundred representatives including Zhu Xuefan, Li Yongxiang, Ye Gonglun, Liu Jintai, Zhou Xuexiang, Chen Peide, Yu Zhengting, Liu Xinquan, Shao Xubai, and Long Peiyun attended.

Congress Staff: Zhu Xuefan, Li Yongxiang, Zhou Xuexiang, Ye Xianggao, and Ge Fei were publicly elected as the presidium; Shao Xubai was the secretary; Long Peiyun was the recorder; Zhao Zhenhui was the emcee; and Li Mengnan, Zhu Xizhang, Liu Zupei, Liu Xinquan, and Fan Yifeng were the reception staff.

Congress Order: (1) Publicly elect the chairman, (2) All stand at attention and sing the Party song, (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and national flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, (4) Read Sun Yat-sen's will respectfully, (5) Observe a moment of silence in mourning for the anti-Japanese martyrs and compatriots who died in the disaster, (6) Chairman's report, (7) Instructions from representatives of higher authorities, (8) Discussion of proposals, (9) Provisional motions, (10) Representatives' speeches, (11) Chanting slogans, (12) Adjournment.

Chairman's Report: After the ceremony, Li Yongxiang reported, "Today, the General Labor Union has convened this representative congress. Looking back from September 18th to now, the national crisis is deepening and the nation is becoming more dangerous. Now that Yuguan has fallen and Tianjin and Beijing are shaken, the central government has resolved to resist. We, the people, should concentrate our efforts and cooperate with the government. Therefore, we have specially convened this representative congress today, hoping to awaken the entire city's labor community to rise up together to defeat Japanese imperialism and save the serious national crisis." Then, Zhu Xuefan reported on the work of the General Labor Union in the year since its establishment and its participation in anti-Japanese work during the Shanghai War.

Proposals Passed: After the chairman's report, discussions began, and the following important proposals were passed: A. Regarding anti-Japanese matters: (1) Send telegrams of condolence to Zhang Xueliang, the anti-Japanese soldiers in North China, and the commanders and all soldiers of the Northeast Volunteer Army. (2) Send a telegram to Chairman Chiang requesting him to transfer elite troops to the front lines to resist the enemy as soon as possible. (3) Send a telegram to national party, government, and military leaders urging them to unite in spirit to resist foreign aggression together. (4) Send a circular telegram to the military governors of all provinces, ordering them to prepare for dispatch and await orders to resist the enemy. (5) Send a telegram of condolence to the Chinese delegation in Geneva. (6) Send a telegram requesting the National Government to declare an economic severance with Japan in accordance with the League of Nations covenant. (7) Pass the motion of expanding the anti-Japanese movement and continuing to actively boycott Japanese goods through mass organizations in provinces, cities, and counties. (8) How should we actively resist Japan? It was resolved that: A. The Shanghai General Labor Union should initiate the organization of a joint office for anti-Japanese organizations from the labor community across the country. B. The Shanghai General Labor Union should initiate the restoration of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese General Organization. C. A notice should be sent to all industry labor unions in the city, instructing all workers and their families not to buy Japanese goods. (9) Issue a circular to all industry labor unions in the city to hold member congresses regularly to carry out anti-Japanese propaganda. (10) Issue a circular to all industry labor unions in the city, instructing workers to donate one day's wages to purchase a "Shanghai Workers" aircraft and send it to the military authorities to resist the enemy. (At the scene, the Fifth District Cotton Textile Labor Union proposed to donate two days' wages from last year's commemorative festival.) (11) Issue a circular to all industry labor unions in the city, instructing workers to actively strive for production, eliminate labor-management disputes, and jointly save the country from destruction during this time of national crisis. (12) Send a telegram requesting overseas party, government, and military leaders to return to the country as soon as possible to jointly preside over the anti-Japanese movement. B. Regarding labor movement matters: (1) The term of office of the executive and supervisory committee members of the General Labor Union has expired and a re-election should be held immediately. (2) The General Labor Union's financial planning. (3) Submit a request to the central government to quickly amend the Trade Union Law and determine the General Labor Union's organization. (4) Send letters to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the National Goods Industry Unions and other organizations, urging them not to close factories or dismiss workers on the pretext of the national crisis, and to embrace the spirit of labor-management cooperation, strive for production, and jointly save the country from danger. (5) Submit a request to party and government agencies to restrict and fairly resolve all labor-management disputes that have occurred in the city as soon as possible. (6) Submit a request to party and government agencies to issue a circular to all industry employers in the city, stating that they shall not independently suspend operations or lay off workers without the approval of the authorities.

Elected Committee Members: The results of the on-site election are as follows: Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, Li Yongxiang, Gong Yuting, Ye Xianggao, Long Peiyun, Zhao Zhenhui, Shi Yitang, Shao Xubai, Li Mengyu, Liu Xinquan, Chen Peide, Zhang Linhua, Liu Zupei, Liu Jintai, Shen Jiabin, Lu Shanben, Lu Jiyun, Dong Aosheng, and other nineteen people were elected as executive committee members; Li Hua, Zhang Huiping, Fan Quan, Zhang Zhuyun, Zhang Yuanming, Zhou Qigui, Tai Genfa, and other seven people were elected as alternate executive committee members; Lu Keming, Ge Fei, Zhang Yaoming, Sang Yutang, Ye Gonglun, Fan Yifeng, Zhang Renjun, and other seven people were elected as supervisory committee members; Bao Jiasheng, Ge Yunting, and Yan Quanyun and other three people were elected as alternate supervisory committee members.

Provisional Motions: Several provisional motions were passed at the end: (1) Request the municipal government to publicly announce the Japanese goods sealed by the previous anti-Japanese association and set a date for their destruction. (2) Request the central government to restore the trade union organization. (3) Send a telegram requesting celebrities in opposition to jointly relieve the national crisis. (4) Request the municipal government to determine the minimum wage limit for workers in the city. (5) Request party and government agencies to stop the China Merchants Bureau from reducing staff. (6) The dispute at the Sanyou Factory has not been resolved for a long time: (A) Request the municipal government to severely punish the factory's employers and enforce arbitration. (B) Organize a fundraising team. (C) Request the municipal government to invite other national goods factories to invest in and start work in the factory's buildings and machinery. (7) Issue a congress declaration. (8) Rename the association the Shanghai General Labor Union. Slogans were chanted immediately, and the meeting adjourned.

Congress Declaration: This congress is opening, almost a year since the previous one. Recalling the day the previous congress closed, we created the city-wide General Union. At that time, the September 18th Incident had just occurred, which marked the beginning of an unprecedented national crisis. This congress arose at the right time, responding to the crisis. Externally, we responded to the national crisis, united the city's workers, and served as the government's support in diplomacy and military affairs. Internally, we overcame obstacles, led existing organizations, and maintained an unyielding spirit to struggle arduously. In the past year, although we have experienced the extremes of hardship, looking at the overall situation, the national crisis has become more severe, and looking at the difficulties of the workers, unemployment has become even more serious. Asking ourselves, we cannot but feel ashamed. Now that Yuguan is in urgent need of help, Tianjin and Beijing are shaken, and the volunteer armies inside and outside the pass are fighting in the severe cold below zero degrees. Looking at the international situation, it is vastly different from the past. Postponing and watching is like revealing our lungs and liver. Japanese imperialism is instigating warlords, sharpening their knives, and pressing forward step by step, with the aim of destroying our race and exterminating our people. This is truly a time when the enemy's knife is at our throat, and we will be killed in an instant. Recalling the past, focusing on current difficulties, and looking to the future, this congress cannot help but feel pain and shed tears. However, what this congress deeply worries about is not the difficulty of the environment, but the dying of the nation and the obliteration of national consciousness. If you do not see who it is that has been jointly responding to the national crisis since the September 18th Incident in Shenyang, it is those who mislead the country and protect themselves, cleverly disguise themselves, take the national crisis as a pretext, and hold the national crisis as a talisman to consolidate their territory. Those who usurp positions are eager to advocate peace and take advantage of the opportunity to seize power, using the national crisis to achieve their own goals. There are also those who take advantage of the national crisis to hoard and speculate, and treacherous people who take advantage of the national crisis to sell their reputation. Short-sighted capitalists take the opportunity to suspend operations and dismiss workers, trapping them in difficult situations. As for puppets and traitors, they are happy to see the national crisis and actively seek to achieve their goals. And there is no need to mention them further. If this is how we jointly respond to the national crisis, it is no wonder that the national crisis is increasing day by day and month by month. National crisis, oh national crisis, how much of China's territory, rights, and lives have been sacrificed in your name? Therefore, if we sincerely want to save the nation from its calamity in the future, we must work hard from top to bottom, seek truth from facts, and not allow any false steps. Commerce must be commerce, labor must be labor, agriculture must be well-cultivated, learning must be accurate, and party and government must strictly enforce discipline, guiding with norms. Each must fulfill their duties in their respective positions, and then the entire country will be orderly and unified, and there will be hope for the country. If there is temporary disturbance and each seeks his own goals, it will be more harmful than beneficial to the country. This is what this congress has sincerely and wholeheartedly hoped to awaken all the people of the country to work together. As for the many ways to save the country, they cannot be exhausted in one article. This congress must supervise and urge the executive and supervisory committee members of this session and all the workers in the city to continue the spirit of the previous session and make earnest efforts, especially in building aviation, consolidating national defense, and providing military training and aid to volunteer armies, which are considered to be the current key tasks. We hope to follow the lead of all sectors and realize them in the shortest possible time. We respectfully submit this humble statement, hoping for your clear guidance. This is the declaration.

The Ministries of Communications and Railways Plan to Raise Funds for Disaster Relief and Cancel the Method of Adding Disaster Relief Donations to Railway and Telegraph Charges 138

Administrative Yuan Replies to Yizhen Association's Telegram

Guowen News Agency reports that the Shanghai Temporary Yizhen Association for Disaster Relief in the Henan, Anhui, and Hubei disaster areas previously proposed adding disaster relief donations to railway and telegraph charges to mortgage large amounts of money and distribute it for emergency relief, as the disaster areas in the three provinces were in urgent need of relief and the collection of relief funds was difficult. This proposal was reviewed and revised by the Commander-in-Chief of the Suppression of Bandits in the Three Provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, and telegraphed to the Administrative Yuan and the Ministries of Communications and Railways for review and handling. The association received a reply telegram from the Administrative Yuan yesterday, which read: "Your telegram has been noted. The Commander-in-Chief of the Three Provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei has requested to add disaster relief donations to railway and telegraph charges because the recovered bandit areas are in urgent need of relief. The Yuan has carefully considered this matter. This method yields little revenue and is also complicated. The Ministries of Communications and Railways should find other ways to raise 500,000 yuan to be used for disaster relief in the bandit-stricken areas of Shaanxi and other provinces. The original plan to add disaster relief donations to railway and telegraph charges can be dismissed. This was proposed and passed by the 83rd Yuan meeting with the resolution: 'Pass. The Ministry of Railways will first issue 200,000 yuan, and the remaining 300,000 yuan will be borne by the Ministry of Railways (250,000 yuan) and the Ministry of Communications (50,000 yuan).' In addition to ordering the Ministries of Railways and Communications to comply with the fundraising and allocation, this is a special reply. (Signed) Song Ziwen, Acting President of the Administrative Yuan."

The British Boxer Indemnity Financial Committee Will Meet Today 143

To Continue Discussing the Loan to the Ministry of Railways

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee, due to the Ministry of Railways' loan case for the completion of the Yuehan Railway, has now received a reply and decided to convene a meeting of the committee's financial committee at No. 1 Jiujiang Road at 4:00 PM today to discuss the remaining loan of 1.2 million pounds. The committee will also continue its previous resolution to appoint Chinese Director Ye Gongchuo and Western Director Turner to attend the meeting in order to study an appropriate method and then submit it to the general meeting for discussion. It is reported that the Ministry of Railways' loan to the committee for the completion of the Yuehan Railway totals 2.4 million pounds. Among them, a portion was already approved by the general meeting on December 5th of last year and issued as public bonds worth 1.2 million gold pounds. The remaining 1.2 million pounds were not decided on at that time because the Ministry of Railways previously had a loan relationship with the British Bank Corporation, which still needed to be negotiated by the Ministry of Railways itself. Recently, the committee received a reply from the Ministry of Railways and convened the financial committee again to continue studying the remaining loan method in order to complete the entire work of the Yuehan Railway as soon as possible. It is reported that Chairman Zhu Jiahua, Vice Chairman Mazar, Chairman of the Financial Committee Hui Rongfu, and others will all participate in the discussion.

Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of Railways, also gave a talk to a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter yesterday, saying that the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee decided to expedite the completion of the Yuehan and Tongxi Railways. The ministry is actively preparing. The Tongxi Railway has already been built to Huayin and will be built to Weinan in July or August of this year. If there are sufficient funds, it can be connected to Xi'an by the end of the year. Among the Zhushao sections of the Yuehan Railway, the section from Shaoguan to Lechang will soon be open to traffic. The entire section is expected to be completed within four years. The Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee expressed satisfaction with the Ministry of Railways' responsible transportation operations. The ministry is determined to work hard and improve daily to facilitate commercial transportation. The Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee also hopes that the Ministry of Railways will expedite the construction of the two railways. The ministry believes that this matter is of great importance and has requested the Administrative Yuan to appoint representatives from the military, political, internal affairs, railways, and Shanghai municipal government departments to plan together. A meeting has been held once, and the representatives of each department have expressed their support for the Ministry of Railways' plan. The detailed method has not yet been determined. As for Mr. Wang Jingwei's recent situation, according to what I have heard, Mr. Wang is still in Europe and has not fully recovered. He was upset by the bad news from Shanhaiguan and decided to return to the country early. He will set off as soon as his health allows him to travel, but the date of departure has not yet been determined.

The Central Government Clarifies the Ambiguity of Article 19 of the Chamber of Commerce Law 145

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce received an order from the Executive Committee of the Municipal Party Headquarters, forwarding the Central Government's explanation of the ambiguity of Article 19 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, and a copy of the original letter from the Central Secretariat to the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee. The original text is recorded below: "The letter from the Judicial Yuan No. 831 states, 'The Shandong Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee has submitted a request from the Licheng County Consolidation Committee to explain the ambiguity of Article 19 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. The Court has already made a unified interpretation of laws and regulations at a plenary meeting. (1) According to Article 18, Paragraph 2 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, since the standing committee members are elected by the executive committee members and appointed from among the standing committee members, the standing committee members and chairman should also be re-elected when half of the executive committee members are re-elected every two years. (2) The lottery re-election in Article 19, Paragraph 2 of the Chamber of Commerce Law is originally limited to the first time. Therefore, when the committee members who remained from the previous session are re-elected after four years, the term of office of the committee members who were elected through the re-election is only two years, and they will not be re-elected at the same time because of this. (3) Although the term of office of the committee members who were re-elected by lottery for the first time is only two years, if they are re-elected at the same time, they are considered to be re-elected as mentioned in this article.' The letter should be replied accordingly for reference." This was approved, and after the Standing Committee members approved, the order was known and the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee was informed. "It is noted that this case was previously submitted to the association by the Shandong Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee, and the Court was instructed to provide an explanation. Now, it has been approved as before and approved above. In addition to the association's instructions, the original submission and the original copy are specially sent to you for your reference. Sincerely, to the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee."

In the Midst of Sino-Russian Resumption of Diplomatic Relations, Japanese Sugar is Sold at Reduced Prices 148

Shensdhi News Agency's local news reports that in the past two weeks, Japanese merchant ships have transported a large batch of white sugar, amounting to 35,000 dan, to Shanghai and started to dump it on a large scale. As a result, the price of genuine Dutch sugar has also fallen. It is investigated that the cause of the large-scale dumping of Japanese sugar at low prices is that they expect the Yuyu incident to expand, and it is heard that Sino-Russian diplomatic relations will be restored and a large batch of refined sugar from Soviet Russia will arrive in Shanghai, so they are selling at reduced prices and even transporting it to the Yangtze River area for dumping.

At present, the nations of the East and West are becoming increasingly close, but the biggest obstacle to goodwill lies in the often unclear understanding of each other's backgrounds. What newspapers record is usually news about wars, accidents, or extraordinary events. Seldom are the true lives, customs, and thoughts of the people revealed. Therefore, the editors of the newspapers he represents deeply believe that there is a vast range of narratives about the people of this region that can be gathered and contributed to the readers. Thus, he has come to China to investigate the trends of the Chinese national economy and politics, and the facts that sufficiently shape the internal conditions and background of future national thought.

Shanghai-Peiping Air Route Resumes Nanking Station 153

| Increased Postage to be Implemented Next Month |

The Shanghai-Peiping air route of the China National Aviation Corporation originally passed through Nanking, Haichow, Tsingtao, Tientsin, and then to Peiping. The company, due to shorter daylight hours in winter, found that flying from Shanghai to Peiping with multiple stops would make it impossible to reach Peiping on time. Therefore, when the route took off for the second time, it only briefly stopped at Haichow, Tsingtao, and Tientsin, flying directly to Peiping without turning to Nanking to save time. This was reported to the Ministry of Communications. However, as the number of mails sent from Shanghai-Hankow to Peiping and Tientsin is increasing daily, to facilitate transportation, it has been decided that starting from the third flight, the original Nanking station air route will be restored. As for the issue of increased postage for airmail, it has been approved by the Executive Yuan, with an increase of ten cents per postal zone (i.e., a total of twenty-five cents), which is scheduled to be implemented starting next month.

Thieves on North Fukien Road Resist Arrest, Bullets Fly

Six Thieves in Tai An Li Search and Rob, Scatter and Flee upon Hearing Police Whistle 154

| One Thief on North Fukien Road Shot and Arrested |

Yesterday at 5:30 PM, a robbery occurred in Tai An Li on North Shansi Road. Afterwards, detectives captured a thief on Fukien Road. Both sides exchanged fire and accidentally injured a passerby. The findings of the investigation are recorded below:

Six Thieves Arrive Suddenly 155

No. 35 Tai An Li is a three-story building. The eastern wing downstairs is the Li Tai Kee Construction Company. The eastern wing upstairs is occupied by the family members of the factory owner. The western wing downstairs is the Hsieh Hsing Metal Company, which is run by Yu Hsing-tsai from Ningpo. His family members live in the western wing upstairs. The middle of the hall upstairs is rented by Hsu Chi-liang, who works at the Tung Yi Company, and his family. At about 5:30 PM yesterday, six thieves suddenly came to the company. Three thieves entered through the front door, and the rest entered through the back door, leaving two thieves to stand guard at the front and back doors. The four thieves then each held a handgun and rushed into the east and west wings.

Simultaneous Search and Robbery in Both Wings 156

When the thieves rushed into the Li Tai Kee Construction Company in the east wing, they immediately forbade everyone from making noise and ordered them to hand over everything they had. However, none of the friends had anything to offer. The thieves then searched their persons. At that time, the factory owner's wife happened to be in the wing and was robbed of two emerald rings, one ruby ring, two jade bracelets, and more than ten yuan in paper money. At the same time, the other thieves broke into the Hsieh Hsing Metal Company in the west wing and searched and robbed in the same way. In total, they robbed 395 silver dollars, 100 small coins, more than ten yuan in paper money, and rings, etc. Seeing that they had searched and robbed everything, the thieves called to each other and drove the people in both wings into the rear room of the east wing and locked them up, assigning one thief to guard them.

Diamond Ring Evades Thief's Notice 157

At this time, Li Chi-liang's wife in the hall upstairs heard footsteps downstairs and went downstairs to take a look. Before she could reach the middle of the staircase, she was spotted by the thieves and forced downstairs. The thieves demanded money from her. She took out 15 yuan in paper money from her pocket. However, Mrs. Li still had valuable watches and diamond rings on her right hand, which fortunately were not noticed by the thieves. Mrs. Li quickly sat down in a hidden place in the hall and secretly took off the diamond ring and put it away, thus avoiding being robbed. Seeing Mrs. Li sitting down, the thieves swarmed upstairs and first entered the hall upstairs to open boxes and chests, but found nothing. Finally, seeing that the drawers on the redwood dressing table were locked, the thieves planned to pry them open. Just then, the owner of Li Tai Kee in the east wing walked out of the room. Seeing this, he knew things were not good and quickly returned to the room and locked the door.

Police Whistle Scares Away Thieves 158

The owner of Li Tai Kee, having closed the door tightly, then pushed open the window and blew the police whistle wildly. The thieves upstairs and downstairs heard this and hurriedly ran out. Two thieves escaped through the front door, firing several shots into the sky to show their strength. The two thieves guarding the front and back doors also fled afterwards. Two thieves, fearing that something was wrong due to the gunshots at the front door, changed course and escaped through the back door. At this time, the people who had been imprisoned by the perpetrators also broke out and chased after them, shouting "Catch the robbers" and pursuing closely. Seeing that they were being chased closely, the two thieves ran through three alleys and across the Old Zha Bridge. It happened that Western detectives No. 50 and Nos. 2371, 2479, from the Division were patrolling the area. Seeing this, they went forward to arrest them.

One Thief Shot and Captured 159

When the detectives chased to the front of the Shanghai Telephone Company on Fukien Road, they were still more than ten yards away from the two thieves. In desperation, the two thieves turned around and fired at the detectives. The detectives returned fire. Bullets flew everywhere, and pedestrians rushed to avoid them. One thief was wounded and fell to the ground and was captured on the spot. A pistol was also seized. One thief escaped in the chaos. At the same time, a person named Ren Ting, from Shaoshing, 17 years old, and an electrician, was hit in the right arm by a stray bullet. He was taken to the Tongren Hospital by the detectives for treatment. The wounded thief and pistol were taken to the police station. Under strict interrogation, he confessed that his name was Chang A-fu, from Kiangyin, 19 years old, and formerly a blacksmith. Before the robbery, someone instigated him and discussed it in room 311 of the Antung Hotel on Hupeh Road. After obtaining the confession, the police dispatched detectives to search everywhere and sent the wounded thief to Tongren Hospital. He had one gunshot wound in his right leg and one in his left waist, with the bullet still in his waist. His life is in danger.

Russian Oil Shipped to Shanghai Continuously 161

Gasoline Market to Have Unprecedented Price Drop

The Ta Lu Pao reports that the local gasoline market will have an unprecedented price drop and competition. Since the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, starting from New Year's Day this year, customs has allowed Soviet ships to fly the Russian flag into port. Previously, Russian kerosene had to be transported to Shanghai on British and German tankers. In the future, it can be loaded on Russian tankers and sailed directly to Shanghai from the Black Sea coast, with one ship arriving in Shanghai approximately every two months, each ship carrying 6 to 8 million gallons of oil. With the abundant supply of Russian oil, the Kwang Hua Company, which distributes it, is also greatly expanding its oil storage facilities in Shanghai and Pudong, adding oil tanks, warehouses, and pumps, etc., and will increase its capital from 1.5 million yuan to 3 million yuan next month. At the same time, it has huge sales plans for gasoline, kerosene, and diesel oil, etc. It is said that its selling price, no matter how other companies compete, will ultimately be five cents per gallon cheaper than the common market price. Devilish Tricks

Bandits Commit All Kinds of Evil, Cleverly Using the "Stealing the Sky and Swapping the Sun" Scheme 166

Gluing White Paper on Envelopes is a Very Clever Scheme, Using Postmarks to Commit Evil is an Innovative Approach

Recently, there has been a type of bandit who specializes in impersonating investigators of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Drug Enforcement Department to scare residents and swindle money. Their technique is very clever and not easy to detect. For example, if they want to extort money from someone, they write a letter reporting that the person has opium paraphernalia or smokes opium in private, and on the front of the envelope, they write the name and address of their accomplice and mail it. After receiving the letter, the accomplice removes the paper glued to the envelope, leaving a blank envelope. Then, they fill in "To Mr. So-and-so, Investigator of the Drug Enforcement Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council." The back of the envelope has already been stamped by the post office. These people then use this letter to claim to those they want to scare that someone has reported them for smoking opium, so they have come to search. When speaking, they show the letter with the postmark. If the person does have an opium addiction or has opium paraphernalia, seeing the letter with the postmark, they will not suspect that it is fake. These people then take the opportunity to extort money, and they are successful almost every time, rarely being exposed. Recently, Hsu Chien-chuan, Hsu Chang-lin, and Hsu's wife Chu, who live at No. 563 Parker Road, also encountered six or seven of these bandits who broke into their home. After finding a smoking pipe, they began to negotiate. Then, Chang Shun-chang, an accomplice of the bandits, arrived uninvited and pretended to mediate, saying that they were all friends and could settle privately. He then extorted 20 yuan in paper money and gave it to the bandits posing as investigators. After they left, Hsu and others initially did not know the inside story and were extremely grateful to Chang, and compensated him with 20 yuan. Later, Chen Yao-ting, an investigator of the Drug Enforcement Department, found out about this and inquired about the whereabouts of the bandits from Hsu Chien-chuan and others. He then went to No. 137 Hsin Zha Road and arrested Chang Shun-chang, and then went to Room 20, Aido Hotel, Aido Road and arrested three accomplices, Hsu Yuan-kuei, Lu Rong-kuei, and Wu Shih-ching, and confiscated fake letters and other items. The day before yesterday, they were escorted to the First Special District District Court, where Judge Chien Wen-chi examined them. Wang Yao-tang, the police lawyer, said that the case committed by the defendants was probably not just once and requested a postponement for detailed investigation. Judge Chien then ordered the defendants to be returned to custody and postponed the trial.

Securities and Goods Exchange Shareholders Meeting 167

Inland River Ships Delayed by Snow Resume Service Yesterday 168

Police Strictly Crack Down on Soochow Creek Ruffians, Temporarily Suspending All But Through Tickets

The Kiangsu and Chekiang inland river ships, which had been delayed and suspended due to the cold weather, heavy snow, and frozen waterways, have now completely resumed service since yesterday after the weather cleared and the shipping companies took measures to break the ice. In addition, the Public Concession Police has also taken action to crack down on the ruffians in the Soochow Creek area. The details are recorded below:

Service Resumed After Weather Clears: The Shanghai-Soochow service of China Merchants Yuan Tung Inland River Small Steamers, the Changshu-Hangchow service of Yuan Tung, the Shanghai-Changshu service of Lao Kung Mao Hsieh Hsing Tai, the Soochow-Changshu service of Lao Kung Mao, the Chingyangkiang-Changshu service of China Merchants, the Soochow-Huchow service of Transportation, the Wusih-Liyang-Kiangyin service of China Merchants Chunghua, and the Changshu-Taitsang service of China Merchants, which had been temporarily suspended due to heavy snow and frozen waterways, causing inconvenience to passengers, have completely resumed service since yesterday after the weather cleared and the companies hired workers to break the ice. The Shanghai-Huchow service of China Merchants Yuan Tung Cheng Chang Li Hsing Li Hsing Yung Shun Yung An, the Shanghai-Pinghu service of Ping Hu Min Nan, the Shanghai-Tsingpu service of Yu Ching, the Shanghai-Changyen service of Shen Chang Hu Chang, and the Shanghai-Sheng Tse service of Ning Shao, which had been running slower and frequently delayed due to the weather, have also returned to normal after the weather cleared.

Crackdown on Ruffians: The wharves along the Soochow Creek are where inland river ships dock. Considering that the ruffians extort money and affect the safety of passengers when the ships arrive, the Lake Society sent a letter to the Inland River Shipping Association, requesting that it take measures to rectify the situation. The association then requested the Public Concession Police to take effective action, which the police verified to be true and ordered the Old Zha and Hueisi police stations to handle it. Since it was implemented last month, with Chinese detectives stationed at each wharf to arrest and send ruffians to the police, ruffians who specialize in extortion have disappeared.

Suspension for Closing Accounts: A reporter from the New Sound Society met with a director of the Inland River Shipping Association yesterday. According to him, the 25th of this month (i.e., the end of the lunar year) is the closing date for the 21st year of various industries. The shipping companies are busy closing accounts, and according to the old practice of previous years, all Jiangsu and Chekiang inland river ships, except those with through-ticket connections with the Shanghai-Nanking and Shanghai-Hangchow Railway passenger trains, will be temporarily suspended from the 24th of this month and will gradually resume service from the 28th.

Preparations for the Great Harmony Music Society's Western Music Tour 169

The Shanghai Great Harmony Music Society recently decided to participate in the Chicago World's Fair in the United States in response to a request from the preparatory office. It was originally planned to transport all 180 kinds of musical instruments it had made to the United States for competition. However, at a meeting of the Standing Committee of the World Academy last Sunday, it was pointed out that transporting the instruments to the United States would be a long and inconvenient journey. Moreover, without members accompanying them to perform, it would be like antiques, which would be boring. Therefore, it was decided to use films and photos of musical instruments for projection and display, which would be more meaningful. The Society then convened a meeting of all members of the Great Orchestra last Sunday afternoon to discuss the preparation methods. The organization was divided into five departments to actively proceed. The Society also adopted a large-scale plan to represent the nature of ancient and modern Chinese music. The program is divided into two categories: (A) Instrumental music (court music, banquet music, chamber music, Buddhist music, Taoist music); (B) Vocal music (folk music, Kunqu opera, Wu songs, southern tunes, northern tunes). The society will invite famous groups and experts from both local and out-of-town areas. Those who are not acquainted only need to judge themselves to have considerable talent and can join on their own. The society welcomes all of them. All office staff have been assigned and are responsible for their respective duties. It is scheduled to officially start work next Monday. This is the first time that Chinese music has been seen by the world, which is of great importance to the inherent culture. It is heard that the members of the society are all working hard.
